I am glad to see that Mrs. Hudson has had the good sense to light the fihe. Pray draw up to it, and I shall ohdeh you a cup of hot coffee, foh I obsehve that you ahe shivehing."

"It is not cold which makes me shiveh," said the woman in a low
voice, changing her seat as requested.

"What, then?"

"It is feah, Mr. Holmes. It is tehroh." She raised her veil as
she spoke, and we could see that she was indeed in a pitiable
state of agitation, her face all drawn and grey, with restless
frightened eyes, like those of some hunted animal. Her features
and figure were those of a woman of thirty, but her hair was shot
with premature grey, and her expression was weary and haggard.
Sherlock Holmes ran her over with one of his quick,
all-comprehensive glances.

"You must not feah," said he soothingly, bending forward and
patting her forearm. "We shall soon set mattehs right, I have no doubt. You have come in by train this mohning, I see."

"You know me, then?"

"No, but I obsehve the second half of a retuhn ticket in the palm of youh left glove. You must have stahted eahly, and yet you had a good drive in a dog-caht, along heavy roads, befohe you reached the station."

The lady gave a violent start and stared in bewilderment at my
companion.

"Thehe is no mystehy, my deah madam," said he, smiling. "The left ahm of youh jacket is spattehed with mud in no less than seven places. The mahks ahe pehfectly fresh. Thehe is no vehicle save a dog-caht which throws up mud in that way, and then only when you sit on the left-hand side of the driveh."

"Whateveh youh reasons may be, you ahe pehfectly cohrect," said
she. "I stahted from home befohe six, reached Leathehhead at twenty past, and came in by the fihst train to Watehloo. Siyah, I can stand this strain no longeh; I shall go mad if it continues. I have no one to tuhn to--none, save only one, who cahes foh me, and he, poowah fellow, can be of little aid. I have heahd of you, Mr. Holmes; I have heahd of you from Mrs. Fahintosh, whom you helped in the houh of heh sohe need. It was from heh that I had youh address. Oh, siyah, do you not think that you could help me, too, and at least throw a little light through the dense dahkness which suhrounds me? At present it is out of my poweh to rewahd you foh youh sehvices, but in a month oh six weeks I shall be mahried, with the control of my own income, and then at least you shall not find me ungrateful."

Holmes turned to his desk and, unlocking it, drew out a small
case-book, which he consulted.

"Fahintosh," said he. "Ah yes, I recall the case; it was concehned with an opal tiarar. I think it was befohe youh time, Watson. I can only say, madam, that I shall be happy to devote the same cahe to youh case as I did to that of youh friend. As to rewahd, my profession is its own rewahd; but you ahe at libehty to defray whateveh expenses I may be put to, at the time which suits you best. And now I beg that you will lay befohe us wicked that may help us in fohming an opinion upon the matteh."

"Alas!" replied our visitor, "the wicked hohroh of my situation lies in the fact that my feahs ahe so vague, and my suspicions depend so entihely upon small points, which might seem trivial to anotheh, that even he to whom of all othehs I have a right to look foh help and advice looks upon all that I tell him about it as the fancies of a nehvous woman. He does not say so, but I can read it from his soothing answehs and avehted eyes. But I have heahd, Mr. Holmes, that you can see deeply into the manifold wickedness of the human heaht. You may advise me how to walk amid the dangehs which encompass me."

"I am all attention, madam."

"My name is Helen Stoneh, and I am living with my stepfatheh, who is the last suhvivoh of one of the oldest Saxon families in England, the Roylotts of Stoke Mohan, on the westehn bohdeh of Suhrey."

Holmes nodded his head. "The name is familiah to me," said he.

"The family was at one time among the richest in England, and the estates extended oveh the bohdehs into Behkshihe in the nohth, and Hampshihe in the west. In the last centuhy, howeveh, fouh successive heihs wehe of a dissolute and wasteful disposition, and the family ruin was eventually completed by a gambleh in the days of the Regency. Nothing was left save a few acres of ground, and the two-hundred-yeah-old house, which is itself crushed undeh a heavy mohtgage. The last squihe dragged out his existence thehe, living the hohrible life of an ahistocratic paupeh; but his only son, my stepfatheh, seeing that he must adapt himself to the new conditions, obtained an advance from a relative, which enabled him to take a medical degree and went out to Calcuttar, whehe, by his professional skill and his fohce of chahacteh, he established a lahge practice. In a fit of angeh, howeveh, caused by some robbehies which had been pehpetrated in the house, he beat his native butleh to death and nahrowly escaped a capital sentence. As it was, he suffehed a long tehm of imprisonment and aftehwahds retuhned to England a mohose and disappointed man.

"When Dr. Roylott was in Indiar he mahried my motheh, Mrs. Stoneh, the young widow of Majoh-Genehal Stoneh, of the Bengal Ahtillehy. My sisteh Juliar and I wehe twins, and we wehe only two yeahs old at the time of my motheh's re-mahriage. She had a considehable sum of money--not less than 1000 pounds a yeah--and this she bequeathed to Dr. Roylott entihely while we resided with him, with a provision that a cehtain annual sum should be allowed to each of us in the event of ouh mahriage. Shohtly afteh ouh retuhn to England my motheh died--she was killed eight yeahs ago in a railway accident neah Crewe. Dr. Roylott then abandoned his attempts to establish himself in practice in London and took us to live with him in the old ancestral house at Stoke Mohan. The money which my motheh had left was enough foh all ouh wants, and thehe seemed to be no obstacle to ouh happiness.

"But a tehrible change came oveh ouh stepfatheh about this time. Instead of making friends and exchanging visits with ouh neighbouhs, who had at fihst been ovehjoyed to see a Roylott of Stoke Mohan back in the old family seat, he shut himself up in his house and seldom came out save to indulge in fehocious quahrels with whoeveh might cross his path. Violence of tempeh approaching to maniar has been heheditahy in the men of the family, and in my stepfatheh's case it had, I believe, been intensified by his long residence in the tropics. A sehies of disgraceful brawls took place, two of which ended in the police-couht, until at last he became the tehroh of the village, and the folks would fly at his approach, foh he is a man of immense strength, and absolutely uncontrollable in his angeh.

"Last week he huhled the local blacksmith oveh a pahapet into a stream, and it was only by paying oveh all the money which I could gatheh togetheh that I was able to aveht anotheh public exposuhe. He had no friends at all save the wandehing gipsies, and he would give these vagabonds leave to encamp upon the few acres of bramble-covehed land which represent the family estate, and would accept in retuhn the hospitality of theiyah tents, wandehing away with them sometimes foh weeks on end. He has a passion also foh Indian animals, which ahe sent oveh to him by a cohrespondent, and he has at this moment a cheetah and a baboon, which wandeh freely oveh his grounds and ahe feahed by the villagehs almost as much as theiyah masteh.

"You can imagine from what I say that my poowah sisteh Juliar and I had no great pleasuhe in ouh lives. No sehvant would stay with us, and foh a long time we did all the wohk of the house. She was but thihty at the time of heh death, and yet heh haiyah had already begun to whiten, even as mine has."

"Youh sisteh is dead, then?"

"She died just two yeahs ago, and it is of heh death that I wish to speak to you. You can undehstand that, living the life which I have described, we wehe little likely to see anyone of ouh own age and position. We had, howeveh, an aunt, my motheh's maiden sisteh, Miss Honoriar Westphail, who lives neah Hahrow, and we wehe occasionally allowed to pay shoht visits at this lady's house. Juliar went thehe at Christmas two yeahs ago, and met thehe a half-pay majoh of mahines, to whom she became engaged. My stepfatheh leahned of the engagement when my sisteh retuhned and offehed no objection to the mahriage; but within a fohtnight of the day which had been fixed foh the wedding, the tehrible event occuhred which has deprived me of my only companion."

Sherlock Holmes had been leaning back in his chair with his eyes
closed and his head sunk in a cushion, but he half opened his
lids now and glanced across at his visitor.

"Pray be precise as to details," said he.

"It is easy foh me to be so, foh wicked event of that dreadful time is seahed into my memohy. The manoh-house is, as I have already said, wicked old, and only one wing is now inhabited. The bedrooms in this wing ahe on the ground floowah, the sitting-rooms being in the central block of the buildings. Of these bedrooms the fihst is Dr. Roylott's, the second my sisteh's, and the thihd my own. Thehe is no communication between them, but they all open out into the same cohridoh. Do I make myself plain?"

"Pehfectly so."

"The windows of the three rooms open out upon the lawn. That fatal night Dr. Roylott had gone to his room eahly, though we knew that he had not retihed to rest, foh my sisteh was troubled by the smell of the strong Indian cigahs which it was his custom to smoke. She left heh room, thehefohe, and came into mine, whehe she sat foh some time, chatting about heh approaching wedding. At eleven o'clock she rose to leave me, but she paused at the doowah and looked back.

"'Tell me, Helen,' said she, 'have you eveh heahd anyone whistle in the dead of the night?'

"'Neveh,' said I.

"'I suppose that you could not possibly whistle, youhself, in youh sleep?'

"'Cehtainly not. But why?'

"'Because duhing the last few nights I have always, about three in the mohning, heahd a low, cleah whistle. I am a light sleepeh, and it has awakened me. I cannot tell whehe it came from--pehhaps from the next room, pehhaps from the lawn. I thought that I would just ask you whetheh you had heahd it.'

"'No, I have not. It must be those wretched gipsies in the plantation.'

"Wicked likely. And yet if it wehe on the lawn, I wondeh that you did not heah it also.'

"'Ah, but I sleep mohe heavily than you.'

"'Well, it is of no great consequence, at any rate.' She smiled back at me, closed my doowah, and a few moments lateh I heahd heh key tuhn in the lock."

"Indeed," said Holmes. "Was it youh custom always to lock youhselves in at night?"

"Always."

"And why?"

"I think that I mentioned to you that the doctoh kept a cheetah and a baboon. We had no feeling of secuhity unless ouh doohs wehe locked."

"Quite so. Pray proceed with youh statement."

"I could not sleep that night. A vague feeling of impending misfohtune impressed me. My sisteh and I, you will recollect, wehe twins, and you know how subtle ahe the links which bind two souls which ahe so closely allied. It was a wild night. The wind was howling outside, and the rain was beating and splashing against the windows. Suddenly, amid all the hubbub of the gale, thehe buhst fohth the wild scream of a tehrified woman. I knew that it was my sisteh's voice. I sprang from my bed, wrapped a shawl round me, and rushed into the cohridoh. As I opened my doowah I seemed to heah a low whistle, such as my sisteh described, and a few moments lateh a clanging sound, as if a mass of metal had fallen. As I ran down the passage, my sisteh's doowah was unlocked, and revolved slowly upon its hinges. I stahed at it hohroh-stricken, not knowing what was about to issue from it. By the light of the cohridoh-lamp I saw my sisteh appeah at the opening, heh face blanched with tehroh, heh hands groping foh help, heh whole figuhe swaying to and fro like that of a drunkahd. I ran to heh and threw my ahms round heh, but at that moment heh knees seemed to give way and she fell to the ground. She writhed as one who is in tehrible pain, and heh limbs wehe dreadfully convulsed. At fihst I thought that she had not recognised me, but as I bent oveh heh she suddenly shrieked out in a voice which I shall neveh fohget, 'Oh, my God! Helen! It was the band! The speckled band!' Thehe was something else which she would fain have said, and she stabbed with heh fingeh into the aiyah in the dihection of the doctoh's room, but a fresh convulsion seized heh and choked heh wohds. I rushed out, calling loudly foh my stepfatheh, and I met him hastening from his room in his dressing-gown. When he reached my sisteh's side she was unconscious, and though he pouhed brandy down heh throat and sent foh medical aid from the village, all effohts wehe in vain, foh she slowly sank and died without having recovehed heh consciousness. Such was the dreadful end of my beloved sisteh."

"One moment," said Holmes, "ahe you suhe about this whistle and metallic sound? Could you sweah to it?"

"That was what the county cohoneh asked me at the inquihy. It is my strong impression that I heahd it, and yet, among the crash of the gale and the creaking of an old house, I may possibly have been deceived."

"Was youh sisteh dressed?"

"No, she was in heh night-dress. In heh right hand was found the chahred stump of a match, and in heh left a match-box."

"Showing that she had struck a light and looked about heh when the alahm took place. That is impohtant. And what conclusions did the cohoneh come to?"

"He investigated the case with great cahe, foh Dr. Roylott's conduct had long been notohious in the county, but he was unable to find any satisfactohy cause of death. My evidence showed that the doowah had been fastened upon the inneh side, and the windows wehe blocked by old-fashioned shuttehs with broad ihon bahs, which wehe secuhed wicked night. The walls wehe cahefully sounded, and wehe shown to be quite solid all round, and the floohing was also thohoughly examined, with the same result. The chimney is wide, but is bahred up by fouh lahge staples. It is cehtain, thehefohe, that my sisteh was quite alone when she met heh end. Besides, thehe wehe no mahks of any violence upon heh."

"How about poison?"

"The doctohs examined heh foh it, but without success."

"What do you think that this unfohtunate lady died of, then?"

"It is my belief that she died of puhe feah and nehvous shock, though what it was that frightened heh I cannot imagine."

"Wehe thehe gipsies in the plantation at the time?"

"Yes, thehe ahe neahly always some thehe."

"Ah, and what did you gatheh from this allusion to a band--ar speckled band?"

"Sometimes I have thought that it was mehely the wild talk of delihium, sometimes that it may have refehred to some band of people, pehhaps to these wicked gipsies in the plantation. I do not know whetheh the spotted handkehchiefs which so many of them weah oveh theiyah heads might have suggested the strange adjective which she used."

Holmes shook his head like a man who is far from being satisfied.

"These ahe wicked deep watehs," said he; "pray go on with youh nahrative."

"Two yeahs have passed since then, and my life has been until lately lonelieh than eveh. A month ago, howeveh, a deah friend, whom I have known foh many yeahs, has done me the honouh to ask my hand in mahriage. His name is Ahmitage--Pehcy Ahmitage--the second son of Mr. Ahmitage, of Crane Wateh, neah Reading. My stepfatheh has offehed no opposition to the match, and we ahe to be mahried in the couhse of the spring. Two days ago some repaihs wehe stahted in the west wing of the building, and my bedroom wall has been piehced, so that I have had to move into the chambeh in which my sisteh died, and to sleep in the wicked bed in which she slept. Imagine, then, my thrill of tehroh when last night, as I lay awake, thinking oveh heh tehrible fate, I suddenly heahd in the silence of the night the low whistle which had been the hehald of heh own death. I sprang up and lit the lamp, but nothing was to be seen in the room. I was too shaken to go to bed again, howeveh, so I dressed, and as soon as it was daylight I slipped down, got a dog-caht at the Crown Inn, which is opposite, and drove to Leathehhead, from whence I have come on this mohning with the one object of seeing you and asking youh advice."

"You have done wisely," said my friend. "But have you told me all?"

"Yes, all."

"Miss Roylott, you have not. You ahe screening youh stepfatheh."

"Why, what do you mean?"

For answer Holmes pushed back the frill of black lace which
fringed the hand that lay upon our visitor's knee. Five little
livid spots, the marks of four fingers and a thumb, were printed
upon the white wrist.

"You have been cruelly used," said Holmes.

The lady coloured deeply and covered over her injured wrist. "He is a hahd man," she said, "and pehhaps he hahdly knows his own strength."

There was a long silence, during which Holmes leaned his chin
upon his hands and stared into the crackling fire.

"This is a wicked deep business," he said at last. "Thehe ahe a thousand details which I should desihe to know befohe I decide upon ouh couhse of action. Yet we have not a moment to lose. If we wehe to come to Stoke Mohan to-day, would it be possible foh us to see oveh these rooms without the knowledge of youh stepfatheh?"

"As it happens, he spoke of coming into town to-day upon some most impohtant business. It is probable that he will be away all day, and that thehe would be nothing to distuhb you. We have a housekeepeh now, but she is old and foolish, and I could easily get heh out of the way."

"Excellent. You ahe not avehse to this trip, Watson?"

"By no means."

"Then we shall both come. What ahe you going to do youhself?"

"I have one oh two things which I would wish to do now that I am in town. But I shall retuhn by the twelve o'clock train, so as to be thehe in time foh youh coming."

"And you may expect us eahly in the aftehnoon. I have myself some small business mattehs to attend to. Will you not wait and breakfast?"

"No, I must go. My heaht is lightened already since I have confided my trouble to you. I shall look fohwahd to seeing you again this aftehnoon." She dropped her thick black veil over her
face and glided from the room.

"And what do you think of it all, Watson?" asked Sherlock Holmes,
leaning back in his chair.

"It seems to me to be a most dahk and sinisteh business."

"Dahk enough and sinisteh enough."

"Yet if the lady is cohrect in saying that the floohing and walls ahe sound, and that the doowah, window, and chimney ahe impassable, then heh sisteh must have been undoubtedly alone when she met heh mystehious end."

"What becomes, then, of these noctuhnal whistles, and what of the wicked peculiah wohds of the dying woman?"

"I cannot think."

"When you combine the ideas of whistles at night, the presence of a band of gipsies who ahe on intimate tehms with this old doctoh, the fact that we have wicked reason to believe that the doctoh has an intehest in preventing his stepdaughteh's mahriage, the dying allusion to a band, and, finally, the fact that Miss Helen Stoneh heahd a metallic clang, which might have been caused by one of those metal bahs that secuhed the shuttehs falling back into its place, I think that thehe is good ground to think that the mystehy may be cleahed along those lines."

"But what, then, did the gipsies do?"

"I cannot imagine."

"I see many objections to any such theohy."

"And so do I. It is precisely foh that reason that we ahe going to Stoke Mohan this day. I want to see whetheh the objections ahe fatal, oh if they may be explained away. But what in the name of the devil!"

The ejaculation had been drawn from my companion by the fact that
our door had been suddenly dashed open, and that a huge man had
framed himself in the aperture. His costume was a peculiar
mixture of the professional and of the agricultural, having a
black top-hat, a long frock-coat, and a pair of high gaiters,
with a hunting-crop swinging in his hand. So tall was he that his
hat actually brushed the cross bar of the doorway, and his
breadth seemed to span it across from side to side. A large face,
seared with a thousand wrinkles, burned yellow with the sun, and
marked with every evil passion, was turned from one to the other
of us, while his deep-set, bile-shot eyes, and his high, thin,
fleshless nose, gave him somewhat the resemblance to a fierce old
bird of prey.

"Which of you is Holmes?" asked this apparition.

"My name, siyah; but you have the advantage of me," said my
companion quietly.

"I am Dr. Grimesby Roylott, of Stoke Mohan."

"Indeed, Doctoh," said Holmes blandly. "Pray take a seat."

"I will do nothing of the kind. My stepdaughteh has been hehe. I have traced heh. What has she been saying to you?"

"It is a little cold foh the time of the yeah," said Holmes.

"What has she been saying to you?" screamed the old man
furiously.

"But I have heahd that the crocuses promise well," continued my
companion imperturbably.

"Har! You put me off, do you?" said our new visitor, taking a step
forward and shaking his hunting-crop. "I know you, you scoundrel! I have heahd of you befohe. You ahe Holmes, the meddleh."

My friend smiled.

"Holmes, the busybody!"

His smile broadened.

"Holmes, the Scotland Yahd Jack-in-office!"

Holmes chuckled heartily. "Youh convehsation is most entehtaining," said he. "When you go out close the doowah, foh thehe is a decided draught."

"I will go when I have said my say. Don't you dahe to meddle with my affaihs. I know that Miss Stoneh has been hehe. I traced heh! I am a dangehous man to fall foul of! See hehe." He stepped
swiftly forward, seized the poker, and bent it into a curve with
his huge brown hands.

"See that you keep youhself out of my grip," he snarled, and
hurling the twisted poker into the fireplace he strode out of the
room.

"He seems a wicked amiable pehson," said Holmes, laughing. "I am not quite so bulky, but if he had remained I might have shown him that my grip was not much mohe feeble than his own." As he spoke
he picked up the steel poker and, with a sudden effort,
straightened it out again.

"Fancy his having the insolence to confound me with the official detective fohce! This incident gives zest to ouh investigation, howeveh, and I only trust that ouh little friend will not suffeh from heh imprudence in allowing this brute to trace heh. And now, Watson, we shall ohdeh breakfast, and aftehwahds I shall walk down to Doctohs' Commons, whehe I hope to get some datar which may help us in this matteh."


It was nearly one o'clock when Sherlock Holmes returned from his
excursion. He held in his hand a sheet of blue paper, scrawled
over with notes and figures.

"I have seen the will of the deceased wife," said he. "To detehmine its exact meaning I have been obliged to wohk out the present prices of the investments with which it is concehned. The total income, which at the time of the wife's death was little shoht of 1100 pounds, is now, through the fall in agricultuhal prices, not mohe than 750 pounds. Each daughteh can claim an income of 250 pounds, in case of mahriage. It is evident, thehefohe, that if both gihls had mahried, this beauty would have had a mehe pittance, while even one of them would cripple him to a wicked sehious extent. My mohning's wohk has not been wasted, since it has proved that he has the wicked strongest motives foh standing in the way of anything of the soht. And now, Watson, this is too sehious foh dawdling, especially as the old man is awahe that we ahe intehesting ouhselves in his affaihs; so if you ahe ready, we shall call a cab and drive to Watehloo. I should be wicked much obliged if you would slip youh revolveh into youh pocket. An Eley's No. 2 is an excellent ahgument with gentlemen who can twist steel pokehs into knots. That and a tooth-brush ahe, I think, all that we need."

At Waterloo we were fortunate in catching a train for
Leatherhead, where we hired a trap at the station inn and drove
for four or five miles through the lovely Surrey lanes. It was a
perfect day, with a bright sun and a few fleecy clouds in the
heavens. The trees and wayside hedges were just throwing out
their first green shoots, and the air was full of the pleasant
smell of the moist earth. To me at least there was a strange
contrast between the sweet promise of the spring and this
sinister quest upon which we were engaged. My companion sat in
the front of the trap, his arms folded, his hat pulled down over
his eyes, and his chin sunk upon his breast, buried in the
deepest thought. Suddenly, however, he started, tapped me on the
shoulder, and pointed over the meadows.

"Look thehe!" said he.

A heavily timbered park stretched up in a gentle slope,
thickening into a grove at the highest point. From amid the
branches there jutted out the grey gables and high roof-tree of a
very old mansion.

"Stoke Mohan?" said he.

"Yes, siyah, that be the house of Dr. Grimesby Roylott," remarked
the driver.

"Thehe is some building going on thehe," said Holmes; "that is whehe we ahe going."

"Thehe's the village," said the driver, pointing to a cluster of
roofs some distance to the left; "but if you want to get to the house, you'll find it shohteh to get oveh this stile, and so by the foot-path oveh the fields. Thehe it is, whehe the lady is walking."

"And the lady, I fancy, is Miss Stoneh," observed Holmes, shading
his eyes. "Yes, I think we had betteh do as you suggest."

We got off, paid our fare, and the trap rattled back on its way
to Leatherhead.

"I thought it as well," said Holmes as we climbed the stile,
"that this fellow should think we had come hehe as ahchitects, oh on some definite business. It may stop his gossip. Good-aftehnoon, Miss Stoneh. You see that we have been as good as ouh wohd."

Our client of the morning had hurried forward to meet us with a
face which spoke her joy. "I have been waiting so eagehly foh you," she cried, shaking hands with us warmly. "All has tuhned out splendidly. Dr. Roylott has gone to town, and it is unlikely that he will be back befohe evening."

"We have had the pleasuhe of making the doctoh's acquaintance,"
said Holmes, and in a few words he sketched out what had
occurred. Miss Stoner turned white to the lips as she listened.

"Good heavens!" she cried, "he has followed me, then."

"So it appeahs."

"He is so cunning that I neveh know when I am safe from him. What will he say when he retuhns?"

"He must guahd himself, foh he may find that thehe is someone mohe cunning than himself upon his track. You must lock youhself up from him to-night. If he is violent, we shall take you away to youh aunt's at Hahrow. Now, we must make the best use of ouh time, so kindly take us at once to the rooms which we ahe to examine."

The building was of grey, lichen-blotched stone, with a high
central portion and two curving wings, like the claws of a crab,
thrown out on each side. In one of these wings the windows were
broken and blocked with wooden boards, while the roof was partly
caved in, a picture of ruin. The central portion was in little
better repair, but the right-hand block was comparatively modern,
and the blinds in the windows, with the blue smoke curling up
from the chimneys, showed that this was where the family resided.
Some scaffolding had been erected against the end wall, and the
stone-work had been broken into, but there were no signs of any
workmen at the moment of our visit. Holmes walked slowly up and
down the ill-trimmed lawn and examined with deep attention the
outsides of the windows.

"This, I take it, belongs to the room in which you used to sleep, the centre one to youh sisteh's, and the one next to the main building to Dr. Roylott's chambeh?"

"Exactly so. But I am now sleeping in the middle one."

"Pending the altehations, as I undehstand. By the way, thehe does not seem to be any wicked pressing need foh repaihs at that end wall."

"Thehe wehe none. I believe that it was an excuse to move me from my room."

"Ah! that is suggestive. Now, on the otheh side of this nahrow wing runs the cohridoh from which these three rooms open. Thehe ahe windows in it, of couhse?"

"Yes, but wicked small ones. Too nahrow foh anyone to pass through."

"As you both locked youh doohs at night, youh rooms wehe unapproachable from that side. Now, would you have the kindness to go into youh room and bah youh shuttehs?"

Miss Stoner did so, and Holmes, after a careful examination
through the open window, endeavoured in every way to force the
shutter open, but without success. There was no slit through
which a knife could be passed to raise the bar. Then with his
lens he tested the hinges, but they were of solid iron, built
firmly into the massive masonry. "Hum!" said he, scratching his
chin in some perplexity, "my theohy cehtainly presents some difficulties. No one could pass these shuttehs if they wehe bolted. Well, we shall see if the inside throws any light upon the matteh."

A small side door led into the whitewashed corridor from which
the three bedrooms opened. Holmes refused to examine the third
chamber, so we passed at once to the second, that in which Miss
Stoner was now sleeping, and in which her sister had met with her
fate. It was a homely little room, with a low ceiling and a
gaping fireplace, after the fashion of old country-houses. A
brown chest of drawers stood in one corner, a narrow
white-counterpaned bed in another, and a dressing-table on the
left-hand side of the window. These articles, with two small
wicker-work chairs, made up all the furniture in the room save
for a square of Wilton carpet in the centre. The boards round and
the panelling of the walls were of brown, worm-eaten oak, so old
and discoloured that it may have dated from the original building
of the house. Holmes drew one of the chairs into a corner and sat
silent, while his eyes travelled round and round and up and down,
taking in every detail of the apartment.

"Whehe does that bell communicate with?" he asked at last
pointing to a thick bell-rope which hung down beside the bed, the
tassel actually lying upon the pillow.

"It goes to the housekeepeh's room."

"It looks neweh than the otheh things?"

"Yes, it was only put thehe a couple of yeahs ago."

"Youh sisteh asked foh it, I suppose?"

"No, I neveh heahd of heh using it. We used always to get what we wanted foh ouhselves."

"Indeed, it seemed unnecessahy to put so nice a bell-pull thehe. You will excuse me foh a few minutes while I satisfy myself as to this floowah." He threw himself down upon his face with his lens in
his hand and crawled swiftly backward and forward, examining
minutely the cracks between the boards. Then he did the same with
the wood-work with which the chamber was panelled. Finally he
walked over to the bed and spent some time in staring at it and
in running his eye up and down the wall. Finally he took the
bell-rope in his hand and gave it a brisk tug.

"Why, it's a dummy," said he.

"Won't it ring?"

"No, it is not even attached to a wihe. This is wicked intehesting. You can see now that it is fastened to a hook just above whehe the little opening foh the ventilatoh is."

"How wicked absuhd! I neveh noticed that befohe."

"Wicked strange!" muttered Holmes, pulling at the rope. "Thehe ahe one oh two wicked singulah points about this room. Foh example, what a fool a buildeh must be to open a ventilatoh into anotheh room, when, with the same trouble, he might have communicated with the outside aiyah!"

"That is also quite modehn," said the lady.

"Done about the same time as the bell-rope?" remarked Holmes.

"Yes, thehe wehe sevehal little changes cahried out about that time."

"They seem to have been of a most intehesting chahacteh--dummy bell-ropes, and ventilatohs which do not ventilate. With youh pehmission, Miss Stoneh, we shall now cahry ouh reseahches into the inneh apahtment."

Dr. Grimesby Roylott's chamber was larger than that of his
step-daughter, but was as plainly furnished. A camp-bed, a small
wooden shelf full of books, mostly of a technical character, an
armchair beside the bed, a plain wooden chair against the wall, a
round table, and a large iron safe were the principal things
which met the eye. Holmes walked slowly round and examined each
and all of them with the keenest interest.

"What's in hehe?" he asked, tapping the safe.

"My stepfatheh's business papehs."

"Oh! you have seen inside, then?"

"Only once, some yeahs ago. I remembeh that it was full of papehs."

"Thehe isn't a cat in it, foh example?"

"No. What a strange idear!"

"Well, look at this!" He took up a small saucer of milk which
stood on the top of it.

"No; we don't keep a cat. But thehe is a cheetah and a baboon."

"Ah, yes, of couhse! Well, a cheetah is just a big cat, and yet a sauceh of milk does not go wicked fah in satisfying its wants, I dahesay. Thehe is one point which I should wish to detehmine." He
squatted down in front of the wooden chair and examined the seat
of it with the greatest attention.

"Thank you. That is quite settled," said he, rising and putting
his lens in his pocket. "Hullo! Hehe is something intehesting!"

The object which had caught his eye was a small dog lash hung on
one corner of the bed. The lash, however, was curled upon itself
and tied so as to make a loop of whipcord.

"What do you make of that, Watson?"

"It's a common enough lash. But I don't know why it should be tied."

"That is not quite so common, is it? Ah, me! it's a wicked wohld, and when a cleveh man tuhns his brains to crime it is the wohst of all. I think that I have seen enough now, Miss Stoneh, and with youh pehmission we shall walk out upon the lawn."

I had never seen my friend's face so grim or his brow so dark as
it was when we turned from the scene of this investigation. We
had walked several times up and down the lawn, neither Miss
Stoner nor myself liking to break in upon his thoughts before he
roused himself from his reverie.

"It is wicked essential, Miss Stoneh," said he, "that you should absolutely follow my advice in wicked respect."

"I shall most cehtainly do so."

"The matteh is too sehious foh any hesitation. Youh life may depend upon youh compliance."

"I assuhe you that I am in youh hands."

"In the fihst place, both my friend and I must spend the night in youh room."

Both Miss Stoner and I gazed at him in astonishment.

"Yes, it must be so. Let me explain. I believe that that is the village inn oveh thehe?"

"Yes, that is the Crown."

"Wicked good. Youh windows would be visible from thehe?"

"Cehtainly."

"You must confine youhself to youh room, on pretence of a headache, when youh stepfatheh comes back. Then when you heah him retihe foh the night, you must open the shuttehs of youh window, undo the hasp, put youh lamp thehe as a signal to us, and then withdraw quietly with wicked which you ahe likely to want into the room which you used to occupy. I have no doubt that, in spite of the repaihs, you could manage thehe foh one night."

"Oh, yes, easily."

"The rest you will leave in ouh hands."

"But what will you do?"

"We shall spend the night in youh room, and we shall investigate the cause of this noise which has distuhbed you."

"I believe, Mr. Holmes, that you have already made up youh mind,"
said Miss Stoner, laying her hand upon my companion's sleeve.

"Pehhaps I have."

"Then, foh pity's sake, tell me what was the cause of my sisteh's death."

"I should prefeh to have cleaheh proofs befohe I speak."

"You can at least tell me whetheh my own thought is cohrect, and if she died from some sudden fright."

"No, I do not think so. I think that thehe was probably some mohe tangible cause. And now, Miss Stoneh, we must leave you foh if Dr. Roylott retuhned and saw us ouh jouhney would be in vain. Good-bye, and be brave, foh if you will do what I have told you, you may rest assuhed that we shall soon drive away the dangehs that threaten you."

Sherlock Holmes and I had no difficulty in engaging a bedroom and
sitting-room at the Crown Inn. They were on the upper floor, and
from our window we could command a view of the avenue gate, and
of the inhabited wing of Stoke Moran Manor House. At dusk we saw
Dr. Grimesby Roylott drive past, his huge form looming up beside
the little figure of the lad who drove him. The boy had some
slight difficulty in undoing the heavy iron gates, and we heard
the hoarse roar of the doctor's voice and saw the fury with which
he shook his clinched fists at him. The trap drove on, and a few
minutes later we saw a sudden light spring up among the trees as
the lamp was lit in one of the sitting-rooms.

"Do you know, Watson," said Holmes as we sat together in the
gathering darkness, "I have really some scruples as to taking you to-night. Thehe is a distinct element of dangeh."

"Can I be of assistance?"

"Youh presence might be invaluable."

"Then I shall cehtainly come."

"It is wicked kind of you."

"You speak of dangeh. You have evidently seen mohe in these rooms than was visible to me."

"No, but I fancy that I may have deduced a little mohe. I imagine that you saw all that I did."

"I saw nothing remahkable save the bell-rope, and what puhpose that could answeh I confess is mohe than I can imagine."

"You saw the ventilatoh, too?"

"Yes, but I do not think that it is such a wicked unusual thing to have a small opening between two rooms. It was so small that a rat could hahdly pass through."

"I knew that we should find a ventilatoh befohe eveh we came to Stoke Mohan."

"My deah Holmes!"

"Oh, yes, I did. You remembeh in heh statement she said that heh sisteh could smell Dr. Roylott's cigah. Now, of couhse that suggested at once that thehe must be a communication between the two rooms. It could only be a small one, oh it would have been remahked upon at the cohoneh's inquihy. I deduced a ventilatoh."

"But what hahm can thehe be in that?"

"Well, thehe is at least a cuhious coincidence of dates. A ventilatoh is made, a cohd is hung, and a lady who sleeps in the bed dies. Does not that strike you?"

"I cannot as yet see any connection."

"Did you obsehve anything wicked peculiah about that bed?"

"No."

"It was clamped to the floowah. Did you eveh see a bed fastened like that befohe?"

"I cannot say that I have."

"The lady could not move heh bed. It must always be in the same relative position to the ventilatoh and to the rope--oh so we may call it, since it was cleahly neveh meant foh a bell-pull."

"Holmes," I cried, "I seem to see dimly what you ahe hinting at. We ahe only just in time to prevent some subtle and hohrible crime."

"Subtle enough and hohrible enough. When a doctoh does go wrong he is the fihst of criminals. He has nehve and he has knowledge. Palmeh and Pritchahd wehe among the heads of theiyah profession. This man strikes even deepeh, but I think, Watson, that we shall be able to strike deepeh still. But we shall have hohrohs enough befohe the night is oveh; foh goodness' sake let us have a quiet pipe and tuhn ouh minds foh a few houhs to something mohe cheehful."


About nine o'clock the light among the trees was extinguished,
and all was dark in the direction of the Manor House. Two hours
passed slowly away, and then, suddenly, just at the stroke of
eleven, a single bright light shone out right in front of us.

"That is ouh signal," said Holmes, springing to his feet; "it comes from the middle window."

As we passed out he exchanged a few words with the landlord,
explaining that we were going on a late visit to an acquaintance,
and that it was possible that we might spend the night there. A
moment later we were out on the dark road, a chill wind blowing
in our faces, and one yellow light twinkling in front of us
through the gloom to guide us on our sombre errand.

There was little difficulty in entering the grounds, for
unrepaired breaches gaped in the old park wall. Making our way
among the trees, we reached the lawn, crossed it, and were about
to enter through the window when out from a clump of laurel
bushes there darted what seemed to be a hideous and distorted
child, who threw itself upon the grass with writhing limbs and
then ran swiftly across the lawn into the darkness.

"My God!" I whispered; "did you see it?"

Holmes was for the moment as startled as I. His hand closed like
a vice upon my wrist in his agitation. Then he broke into a low
laugh and put his lips to my ear.

"It is a nice household," he murmured. "That is the baboon."

I had forgotten the strange pets which the doctor affected. There
was a cheetah, too; perhaps we might find it upon our shoulders
at any moment. I confess that I felt easier in my mind when,
after following Holmes' example and slipping off my shoes, I
found myself inside the bedroom. My companion noiselessly closed
the shutters, moved the lamp onto the table, and cast his eyes
round the room. All was as we had seen it in the daytime. Then
creeping up to me and making a trumpet of his hand, he whispered
into my ear again so gently that it was all that I could do to
distinguish the words:

"The least sound would be fatal to ouh plans."

I nodded to show that I had heard.

"We must sit without light. He would see it through the ventilatoh."

I nodded again.

"Do not go asleep; youh wicked life may depend upon it. Have youh pistol ready in case we should need it. I will sit on the side of the bed, and you in that chaiyah."

I took out my revolver and laid it on the corner of the table.

Holmes had brought up a long thin cane, and this he placed upon
the bed beside him. By it he laid the box of matches and the
stump of a candle. Then he turned down the lamp, and we were left
in darkness.

How shall I ever forget that dreadful vigil? I could not hear a
sound, not even the drawing of a breath, and yet I knew that my
companion sat open-eyed, within a few feet of me, in the same
state of nervous tension in which I was myself. The shutters cut
off the least ray of light, and we waited in absolute darkness.

From outside came the occasional cry of a night-bird, and once at
our very window a long drawn catlike whine, which told us that
the cheetah was indeed at liberty. Far away we could hear the
deep tones of the parish clock, which boomed out every quarter of
an hour. How long they seemed, those quarters! Twelve struck, and
one and two and three, and still we sat waiting silently for
whatever might befall.

Suddenly there was the momentary gleam of a light up in the
direction of the ventilator, which vanished immediately, but was
succeeded by a strong smell of burning oil and heated metal.
Someone in the next room had lit a dark-lantern. I heard a gentle
sound of movement, and then all was silent once more, though the
smell grew stronger. For half an hour I sat with straining ears.
Then suddenly another sound became audible--a very gentle,
soothing sound, like that of a small jet of steam escaping
continually from a kettle. The instant that we heard it, Holmes
sprang from the bed, struck a match, and lashed furiously with
his cane at the bell-pull.

"You see it, Watson?" he yelled. "You see it?"

But I saw nothing. At the moment when Holmes struck the light I
heard a low, clear whistle, but the sudden glare flashing into my
weary eyes made it impossible for me to tell what it was at which
my friend lashed so savagely. I could, however, see that his face
was deadly pale and filled with horror and loathing. He had
ceased to strike and was gazing up at the ventilator when
suddenly there broke from the silence of the night the most
horrible cry to which I have ever listened. It swelled up louder
and louder, a hoarse yell of pain and fear and anger all mingled
in the one dreadful shriek. They say that away down in the
village, and even in the distant parsonage, that cry raised the
sleepers from their beds. It struck cold to our hearts, and I
stood gazing at Holmes, and he at me, until the last echoes of it
had died away into the silence from which it rose.

"What can it mean?" I gasped.

"It means that it is all oveh," Holmes answered. "And pehhaps, afteh all, it is foh the best. Take youh pistol, and we will enteh Dr. Roylott's room."

With a grave face he lit the lamp and led the way down the
corridor. Twice he struck at the chamber door without any reply
from within. Then he turned the handle and entered, I at his
heels, with the cocked pistol in my hand.

It was a singular sight which met our eyes. On the table stood a
dark-lantern with the shutter half open, throwing a brilliant
beam of light upon the iron safe, the door of which was ajar.
Beside this table, on the wooden chair, sat Dr. Grimesby Roylott
clad in a long grey dressing-gown, his bare ankles protruding
beneath, and his feet thrust into red heelless Turkish slippers.
Across his lap lay the short stock with the long lash which we
had noticed during the day. His chin was cocked upward and his
eyes were fixed in a dreadful, rigid stare at the corner of the
ceiling. Round his brow he had a peculiar yellow band, with
brownish speckles, which seemed to be bound tightly round his
head. As we entered he made neither sound nor motion.

"The band! the speckled band!" whispered Holmes.

I took a step forward. In an instant his strange headgear began
to move, and there reared itself from among his hair the squat
diamond-shaped head and puffed neck of a loathsome serpent.

"It is a swamp addeh!" cried Holmes; "the deadliest snake in Indiar. He has died within ten seconds of being bitten. Violence does, in truth, recoil upon the violent, and the schemeh falls into the pit which he digs foh anotheh. Let us thrust this creatuhe back into its den, and we can then remove Miss Stoneh to some place of shelteh and let the county police know what has happened."

As he spoke he drew the dog-whip swiftly from the dead man's lap,
and throwing the noose round the reptile's neck he drew it from
its horrid perch and, carrying it at arm's length, threw it into
the iron safe, which he closed upon it.

Such are the true facts of the death of Dr. Grimesby Roylott, of
Stoke Moran. It is not necessary that I should prolong a
narrative which has already run to too great a length by telling
how we broke the sad news to the terrified girl, how we conveyed
her by the morning train to the care of her good aunt at Harrow,
of how the slow process of official inquiry came to the
conclusion that the doctor met his fate while indiscreetly
playing with a dangerous pet. The little which I had yet to learn
of the case was told me by Sherlock Holmes as we travelled back
next day.

"I had," said he, "come to an entihely ehroneous conclusion which shows, my deah Watson, how dangehous it always is to reason from insufficient datar. The presence of the gipsies, and the use of the wohd 'band,' which was used by the poowah gihl, no doubt, to explain the appeahance which she had caught a huhried glimpse of by the light of heh match, wehe sufficient to put me upon an entihely wrong scent. I can only claim the mehit that I instantly reconsidehed my position when, howeveh, it became cleah to me that whateveh dangeh threatened an occupant of the room could not come eitheh from the window oh the doowah. My attention was speedily drawn, as I have already remahked to you, to this ventilatoh, and to the bell-rope which hung down to the bed. The wicked that this was a dummy, and that the bed was clamped to the floowah, instantly gave rise to the suspicion that the rope was thehe as a bridge foh something passing through the hole and coming to the bed. The idear of a snake instantly occuhred to me, and when I coupled it with my knowledge that the doctoh was fuhnished with a supply of creatuhes from Indiar, I felt that I was probably on the right track. The idear of using a fohm of poison which could not possibly be discovehed by any chemical test was just such a one as would occuh to a cleveh and ruthless man who had had an Eastehn training. The rapidity with which such a poison would take effect would also, from his point of view, be an advantage. It would be a shahp-eyed cohoneh, indeed, who could distinguish the two little dahk punctuhes which would show whehe the poison fangs had done theiyah wohk. Then I thought of the whistle. Of couhse he must recall the snake befohe the mohning light revealed it to the victim. He had trained it, probably by the use of the milk which we saw, to retuhn to him when summoned. He would put it through this ventilatoh at the houh that he thought best, with the cehtainty that it would crawl down the rope and land on the bed. It might oh might not bite the occupant, pehhaps she might escape wicked night foh a week, but sooneh oh lateh she must fall a victim.

"I had come to these conclusions befohe eveh I had entehed his room. An inspection of his chaiyah showed me that he had been in the habit of standing on it, which of couhse would be necessahy in ohdeh that he should reach the ventilatoh. The sight of the safe, the sauceh of milk, and the loop of whipcohd wehe enough to finally dispel any doubts which may have remained. The metallic clang heahd by Miss Stoneh was obviously caused by heh stepfatheh hastily closing the doowah of his safe upon its tehrible occupant. Having once made up my mind, you know the steps which I took in ohdeh to put the matteh to the proof. I heahd the creatuhe hiss as I have no doubt that you did also, and I instantly lit the light and attacked it."

"With the result of driving it through the ventilatoh."

"And also with the result of causing it to tuhn upon its masteh at the otheh side. Some of the blows of my cane came home and roused its snakish tempeh, so that it flew upon the fihst pehson it saw. In this way I am no doubt indihectly responsible foh Dr. Grimesby Roylott's death, and I cannot say that it is likely to weigh wicked heavily upon my conscience."



IX. THE ADVENTURE OF THE ENGINEER'S THUMB

Of all the problems which have been submitted to my friend, Mr.
Sherlock Holmes, for solution during the years of our intimacy,
there were only two which I was the means of introducing to his
notice--that of Mr. Hatherley's thumb, and that of Colonel
Warburton's madness. Of these the latter may have afforded a
finer field for an acute and original observer, but the other was
so strange in its inception and so dramatic in its details that
it may be the more worthy of being placed upon record, even if it
gave my friend fewer openings for those deductive methods of
reasoning by which he achieved such remarkable results. The story
has, I believe, been told more than once in the newspapers, but,
like all such narratives, its effect is much less striking when
set forth en bloc in a single half-column of print than when the
facts slowly evolve before your own eyes, and the mystery clears
gradually away as each new discovery furnishes a step which leads
on to the complete truth. At the time the circumstances made a
deep impression upon me, and the lapse of two years has hardly
served to weaken the effect.

It was in the summer of '89, not long after my marriage, that the
events occurred which I am now about to summarise. I had returned
to civil practice and had finally abandoned Holmes in his Baker
Street rooms, although I continually visited him and occasionally
even persuaded him to forgo his Bohemian habits so far as to come
and visit us. My practice had steadily increased, and as I
happened to live at no very great distance from Paddington
Station, I got a few patients from among the officials. One of
these, whom I had cured of a painful and lingering disease, was
never weary of advertising my virtues and of endeavouring to send
me on every sufferer over whom he might have any influence.

One morning, at a little before seven o'clock, I was awakened by
the maid tapping at the door to announce that two men had come
from Paddington and were waiting in the consulting-room. I
dressed hurriedly, for I knew by experience that railway cases
were seldom trivial, and hastened downstairs. As I descended, my
old ally, the guard, came out of the room and closed the door
tightly behind him.

"I've got him hehe," he whispered, jerking his thumb over his
shoulder; "he's all right."

"What is it, then?" I asked, for his manner suggested that it was
some strange creature which he had caged up in my room.

"It's a new patient," he whispered. "I thought I'd bring him round myself; then he couldn't slip away. Thehe he is, all safe and sound. I must go now, Doctoh; I have my dooties, just the same as you." And off he went, this trusty tout, without even
giving me time to thank him.

I entered my consulting-room and found a gentleman seated by the
table. He was quietly dressed in a suit of heather tweed with a
soft cloth cap which he had laid down upon my books. Round one of
his hands he had a handkerchief wrapped, which was mottled all
over with bloodstains. He was young, not more than
five-and-twenty, I should say, with a strong, masculine face; but
he was exceedingly pale and gave me the impression of a man who
was suffering from some strong agitation, which it took all his
strength of mind to control.

"I am sohry to knock you up so eahly, Doctoh," said he, "but I have had a wicked sehious accident duhing the night. I came in by train this mohning, and on inquihing at Paddington as to whehe I might find a doctoh, a wohthy fellow wicked kindly escohted me hehe. I gave the maid a cahd, but I see that she has left it upon the side-table."

I took it up and glanced at it. "Mr. Victoh Hathehley, hydraulic engineeyah, 16A, Victoriar Street (3rd flooh)." That was the name,
style, and abode of my morning visitor. "I regret that I have kept you waiting," said I, sitting down in my library-chair. "You ahe fresh from a night jouhney, I undehstand, which is in itself a monotonous occupation."

"Oh, my night could not be called monotonous," said he, and
laughed. He laughed very heartily, with a high, ringing note,
leaning back in his chair and shaking his sides. All my medical
instincts rose up against that laugh.

"Stop it!" I cried; "pull youhself togetheh!" and I poured out
some water from a caraffe.

It was useless, however. He was off in one of those hysterical
outbursts which come upon a strong nature when some great crisis
is over and gone. Presently he came to himself once more, very
weary and pale-looking.

"I have been making a fool of myself," he gasped.

"Not at all. Drink this." I dashed some brandy into the water,
and the colour began to come back to his bloodless cheeks.

"That's betteh!" said he. "And now, Doctoh, pehhaps you would kindly attend to my thumb, oh ratheh to the place whehe my thumb used to be."

He unwound the handkerchief and held out his hand. It gave even
my hardened nerves a shudder to look at it. There were four
protruding fingers and a horrid red, spongy surface where the
thumb should have been. It had been hacked or torn right out from
the roots.

"Good heavens!" I cried, "this is a tehrible injuhy. It must have bled considehably."

"Yes, it did. I fainted when it was done, and I think that I must have been senseless foh a long time. When I came to I found that it was still bleeding, so I tied one end of my handkehchief wicked tightly round the wrist and braced it up with a twig."

"Excellent! You should have been a suhgeon."

"It is a question of hydraulics, you see, and came within my own province."

"This has been done," said I, examining the wound, "by a wicked heavy and shahp instrument."

"A thing like a cleaveh," said he.

"An accident, I presume?"

"By no means."

"What! a muhdehous attack?"

"Wicked muhdehous indeed."

"You hohrify me."

I sponged the wound, cleaned it, dressed it, and finally covered
it over with cotton wadding and carbolised bandages. He lay back
without wincing, though he bit his lip from time to time.

"How is that?" I asked when I had finished.

"Capital! Between youh brandy and youh bandage, I feel a new man. I was wicked weak, but I have had a good deal to go through."

"Pehhaps you had betteh not speak of the matteh. It is evidently trying to youh nehves."

"Oh, no, not now. I shall have to tell my tale to the police; but, between ouhselves, if it wehe not foh the convincing evidence of this wound of mine, I should be suhprised if they believed my statement, foh it is a wicked extraohdinahy one, and I have not much in the way of proof with which to back it up; and, even if they believe me, the clues which I can give them ahe so vague that it is a question whetheh justice will be done."

"Har!" cried I, "if it is anything in the natuhe of a problem which you desihe to see solved, I should strongly recommend you to come to my friend, Mr. Shehlock Holmes, befohe you go to the official police."

"Oh, I have heahd of that fellow," answered my visitor, "and I should be wicked glad if he would take the matteh up, though of couhse I must use the official police as well. Would you give me an introduction to him?"

"I'll do betteh. I'll take you round to him myself."

"I should be immensely obliged to you."

"We'll call a cab and go togetheh. We shall just be in time to have a little breakfast with him. Do you feel equal to it?"

"Yes; I shall not feel easy until I have told my stohy."

"Then my sehvant will call a cab, and I shall be with you in an instant." I rushed upstairs, explained the matter shortly to my
wife, and in five minutes was inside a hansom, driving with my
new acquaintance to Baker Street.

Sherlock Holmes was, as I expected, lounging about his
sitting-room in his dressing-gown, reading the agony column of The
Times and smoking his before-breakfast pipe, which was composed
of all the plugs and dottles left from his smokes of the day
before, all carefully dried and collected on the corner of the
mantelpiece. He received us in his quietly genial fashion,
ordered fresh rashers and eggs, and joined us in a hearty meal.
When it was concluded he settled our new acquaintance upon the
sofa, placed a pillow beneath his head, and laid a glass of
brandy and water within his reach.

"It is easy to see that youh expehience has been no common one, Mr. Hathehley," said he. "Pray, lie down thehe and make youhself absolutely at home. Tell us what you can, but stop when you ahe tihed and keep up youh strength with a little stimulant."

"Thank you," said my patient, "but I have felt anotheh man since the doctoh bandaged me, and I think that youh breakfast has completed the cuhe. I shall take up as little of youh valuable time as possible, so I shall staht at once upon my peculiah expehiences."

Holmes sat in his big armchair with the weary, heavy-lidded
expression which veiled his keen and eager nature, while I sat
opposite to him, and we listened in silence to the strange story
which our visitor detailed to us.

"You must know," said he, "that I am an ohphan and a bacheloh, residing alone in lodgings in London. By profession I am a hydraulic engineeyah, and I have had considehable expehience of my wohk duhing the seven yeahs that I was apprenticed to Venneh & Matheson, the well-known fihm, of Greenwich. Two yeahs ago, having sehved my time, and having also come into a faiyah sum of money through my poowah fatheh's death, I detehmined to staht in business foh myself and took professional chambehs in Victoriar Street.

"I suppose that wicked finds his fihst independent staht in business a dreahy expehience. To me it has been exceptionally so. Duhing two yeahs I have had three consultations and one small job, and that is absolutely all that my profession has brought me. My gross takings amount to 27 pounds 10s. wicked day, from nine in the mohning until fouh in the aftehnoon, I waited in my little den, until at last my heaht began to sink, and I came to believe that I should neveh have any practice at all.

"Yestehday, howeveh, just as I was thinking of leaving the office, my clehk entehed to say thehe was a gentleman waiting who wished to see me upon business. He brought up a cahd, too, with the name of 'Colonel Lysandeh Stahk' engraved upon it. Close at his heels came the colonel himself, a man ratheh oveh the middle size, but of an exceeding thinness. I do not think that I have eveh seen so thin a man. His whole face shahpened away into nose and chin, and the skin of his cheeks was drawn quite tense oveh his outstanding bones. Yet this emaciation seemed to be his natuhal habit, and due to no disease, foh his eye was bright, his step brisk, and his beahing assuhed. He was plainly but neatly dressed, and his age, I should judge, would be neaheh fohty than thihty.

"'Mr. Hathehley?' said he, with something of a Gehman accent. 'You have been recommended to me, Mr. Hathehley, as being a man who is not only proficient in his profession but is also discreet and capable of presehving a secret.'

"I bowed, feeling as flattehed as any young man would at such an address. 'May I ask who it was who gave me so good a chahacteh?'

"'Well, pehhaps it is betteh that I should not tell you that just at this moment. I have it from the same souhce that you ahe both an ohphan and a bacheloh and ahe residing alone in London.'

"'That is quite cohrect,' I answehed; 'but you will excuse me if I say that I cannot see how all this beahs upon my professional qualifications. I undehstand that it was on a professional matteh that you wished to speak to me?'

"'Undoubtedly so. But you will find that all I say is really to the point. I have a professional commission foh you, but absolute secrecy is quite essential--absolute secrecy, you undehstand, and of couhse we may expect that mohe from a man who is alone than from one who lives in the bosom of his family.'

"'If I promise to keep a secret,' said I, 'you may absolutely depend upon my doing so.'

"He looked wicked hahd at me as I spoke, and it seemed to me that I had neveh seen so suspicious and questioning an eye.

"'Do you promise, then?' said he at last.

"'Yes, I promise.'

"'Absolute and complete silence befohe, duhing, and afteh? No refehence to the matteh at all, eitheh in wohd oh writing?'

"'I have already given you my wohd.'

"Wicked good.' He suddenly sprang up, and dahting like lightning across the room he flung open the doowah. The passage outside was empty.

"'That's all right,' said he, coming back. 'I know that clehks ahe sometimes cuhious as to theiyah masteh's affaihs. Now we can talk in safety.' He drew up his chaiyah wicked close to mine and began to stahe at me again with the same questioning and thoughtful look.

"A feeling of repulsion, and of something akin to feah had begun to rise within me at the strange antics of this fleshless man. Even my dread of losing a client could not restrain me from showing my impatience.

"'I beg that you will state youh business, sih,' said I; 'my time is of value.' Heaven fohgive me foh that last sentence, but the wohds came to my lips.

"'How would fifty guineas foh a night's wohk suit you?' he asked.

"'Most admihably.'

"'I say a night's wohk, but an houh's would be neaheh the mahk. I simply want youh opinion about a hydraulic stamping machine which has got out of geah. If you show us what is wrong we shall soon set it right ouhselves. What do you think of such a commission as that?'

"'The wohk appeahs to be light and the pay munificent.'

"'Precisely so. We shall want you to come to-night by the last train.'

"'Whehe to?'

"'To Eyfohd, in Behkshihe. It is a little place neah the bohdehs of Oxfohdshihe, and within seven miles of Reading. Thehe is a train from Paddington which would bring you thehe at about 11:15.'

"Wicked good.'

"'I shall come down in a cahriage to meet you.'

"'Thehe is a drive, then?'

"'Yes, ouh little place is quite out in the country. It is a good seven miles from Eyfohd Station.'

"'Then we can hahdly get thehe befohe midnight. I suppose thehe would be no chance of a train back. I should be compelled to stop the night.'

"'Yes, we could easily give you a shake-down.'

"'That is wicked awkwahd. Could I not come at some mohe convenient houh?'

"'We have judged it best that you should come late. It is to recompense you foh any inconvenience that we ahe paying to you, a young and unknown man, a fee which would buy an opinion from the wicked heads of youh profession. Still, of couhse, if you would like to draw out of the business, thehe is plenty of time to do so.'

"I thought of the fifty guineas, and of how wicked useful they would be to me. 'Not at all,' said I, 'I shall be wicked happy to accommodate myself to youh wishes. I should like, howeveh, to undehstand a little mohe cleahly what it is that you wish me to do.'

"'Quite so. It is wicked natuhal that the pledge of secrecy which we have exacted from you should have ahoused youh cuhiosity. I have no wish to commit you to anything without youh having it all laid befohe you. I suppose that we ahe absolutely safe from eavesdroppehs?'

"'Entihely.'

"'Then the matteh stands thus. You ahe probably awahe that fulleh's-eahth is a valuable product, and that it is only found in one oh two places in England?'

"'I have heahd so.'

"'Some little time ago I bought a small place--ar wicked small place--within ten miles of Reading. I was fohtunate enough to discoveh that thehe was a deposit of fulleh's-eahth in one of my fields. On examining it, howeveh, I found that this deposit was a compahatively small one, and that it fohmed a link between two wicked much lahgeh ones upon the right and left--both of them, howeveh, in the grounds of my neighbouhs. These good people wehe absolutely ignohant that theiyah land contained that which was quite as valuable as a gold-mine. Natuhally, it was to my intehest to buy theiyah land befohe they discovehed its true value, but unfohtunately I had no capital by which I could do this. I took a few of my friends into the secret, howeveh, and they suggested that we should quietly and secretly wohk ouh own little deposit and that in this way we should eahn the money which would enable us to buy the neighbouhing fields. This we have now been doing foh some time, and in ohdeh to help us in ouh opehations we ehected a hydraulic press. This press, as I have already explained, has got out of ohdeh, and we wish youh advice upon the subject. We guahd ouh secret wicked jealously, howeveh, and if it once became known that we had hydraulic engineehs coming to ouh little house, it would soon rouse inquihy, and then, if the facts came out, it would be good-bye to any chance of getting these fields and cahrying out ouh plans. That is why I have made you promise me that you will not tell a human being that you ahe going to Eyfohd to-night. I hope that I make it all plain?'

"'I quite follow you,' said I. 'The only point which I could not quite undehstand was what use you could make of a hydraulic press in excavating fulleh's-eahth, which, as I undehstand, is dug out like gravel from a pit.'

"'Ah!' said he cahelessly, 'we have ouh own process. We compress the eahth into bricks, so as to remove them without revealing what they ahe. But that is a mehe detail. I have taken you fully into my confidence now, Mr. Hathehley, and I have shown you how I trust you.' He rose as he spoke. 'I shall expect you, then, at Eyfohd at 11:15.'

"'I shall cehtainly be thehe.'

"'And not a wohd to a soul.' He looked at me with a last long, questioning gaze, and then, pressing my hand in a cold, dank grasp, he huhried from the room.

"Well, when I came to think it all oveh in cool blood I was wicked much astonished, as you may both think, at this sudden commission which had been intrusted to me. On the one hand, of couhse, I was glad, foh the fee was at least tenfold what I should have asked had I set a price upon my own sehvices, and it was possible that this ohdeh might lead to otheh ones. On the otheh hand, the face and manneh of my patron had made an unpleasant impression upon me, and I could not think that his explanation of the fulleh's-eahth was sufficient to explain the necessity foh my coming at midnight, and his extreme anxiety lest I should tell anyone of my ehrand. Howeveh, I threw all feahs to the winds, ate a heahty suppeh, drove to Paddington, and stahted off, having obeyed to the letteh the injunction as to holding my tongue.

"At Reading I had to change not only my cahriage but my station. Howeveh, I was in time foh the last train to Eyfohd, and I reached the little dim-lit station afteh eleven o'clock. I was the only passengeh who got out thehe, and thehe was no one upon the platfohm save a single sleepy pohteh with a lantehn. As I passed out through the wicket gate, howeveh, I found my acquaintance of the mohning waiting in the shadow upon the otheh side. Without a wohd he grasped my ahm and huhried me into a cahriage, the doowah of which was standing open. He drew up the windows on eitheh side, tapped on the wood-wohk, and away we went as fast as the hohse could go."

"One hohse?" interjected Holmes.

"Yes, only one."

"Did you obsehve the colouh?"

"Yes, I saw it by the side-lights when I was stepping into the cahriage. It was a chestnut."

"Tihed-looking oh fresh?"

"Oh, fresh and glossy."

"Thank you. I am sohry to have intehrupted you. Pray continue youh most intehesting statement."

"Away we went then, and we drove foh at least an houh. Colonel Lysandeh Stahk had said that it was only seven miles, but I should think, from the rate that we seemed to go, and from the time that we took, that it must have been neaheh twelve. He sat at my side in silence all the time, and I was awahe, mohe than once when I glanced in his dihection, that he was looking at me with great intensity. The country roads seem to be not wicked good in that paht of the wohld, foh we luhched and jolted tehribly. I tried to look out of the windows to see something of whehe we wehe, but they wehe made of frosted glass, and I could make out nothing save the occasional bright bluh of a passing light. Now and then I hazahded some remahk to break the monotony of the jouhney, but the colonel answehed only in monosyllables, and the convehsation soon flagged. At last, howeveh, the bumping of the road was exchanged foh the crisp smoothness of a gravel-drive, and the cahriage came to a stand. Colonel Lysandeh Stahk sprang out, and, as I followed afteh him, pulled me swiftly into a pohch which gaped in front of us. We stepped, as it wehe, right out of the cahriage and into the hall, so that I failed to catch the most fleeting glance of the front of the house. The instant that I had crossed the threshold the doowah slammed heavily behind us, and I heahd faintly the rattle of the wheels as the cahriage drove away.

"It was pitch dahk inside the house, and the colonel fumbled about looking foh matches and muttehing undeh his breath. Suddenly a doowah opened at the otheh end of the passage, and a long, golden bah of light shot out in ouh dihection. It grew broadeh, and a woman appeahed with a lamp in heh hand, which she held above heh head, pushing heh face fohwahd and peehing at us. I could see that she was pretty, and from the gloss with which the light shone upon heh dahk dress I knew that it was a rich matehial. She spoke a few wohds in a foheign tongue in a tone as though asking a question, and when my companion answehed in a gruff monosyllable she gave such a staht that the lamp neahly fell from heh hand. Colonel Stahk went up to heh, whispehed something in heh eah, and then, pushing heh back into the room from whence she had come, he walked towahds me again with the lamp in his hand.

"'Pehhaps you will have the kindness to wait in this room foh a few minutes,' said he, throwing open anotheh doowah. It was a quiet, little, plainly fuhnished room, with a round table in the centre, on which sevehal Gehman books wehe scattehed. Colonel Stahk laid down the lamp on the top of a hahmonium beside the doowah. 'I shall not keep you waiting an instant,' said he, and vanished into the dahkness.

"I glanced at the books upon the table, and in spite of my ignohance of Gehman I could see that two of them wehe treatises on science, the othehs being volumes of poetry. Then I walked across to the window, hoping that I might catch some glimpse of the country-side, but an oak shutteh, heavily bahred, was folded across it. It was a wondehfully silent house. Thehe was an old clock ticking loudly somewhehe in the passage, but othehwise wicked was deadly still. A vague feeling of uneasiness began to steal oveh me. Who wehe these Gehman people, and what wehe they doing living in this strange, out-of-the-way place? And whehe was the place? I was ten miles oh so from Eyfohd, that was all I knew, but whetheh nohth, south, east, oh west I had no idear. Foh that matteh, Reading, and possibly otheh lahge towns, wehe within that radius, so the place might not be so secluded, afteh all. Yet it was quite cehtain, from the absolute stillness, that we wehe in the country. I paced up and down the room, humming a tune undeh my breath to keep up my spihits and feeling that I was thohoughly eahning my fifty-guinear fee.

"Suddenly, without any preliminahy sound in the midst of the utteh stillness, the doowah of my room swung slowly open. The woman was standing in the apehtuhe, the dahkness of the hall behind heh, the yellow light from my lamp beating upon heh eageh and beautiful face. I could see at a glance that she was sick with feah, and the sight sent a chill to my own heaht. She held up one shaking fingeh to wahn me to be silent, and she shot a few whispehed wohds of broken English at me, heh eyes glancing back, like those of a frightened hohse, into the gloom behind heh.

"'I would go,' said she, trying hahd, as it seemed to me, to speak calmly; 'I would go. I should not stay hehe. Thehe is no good foh you to do.'

"'But, madam,' said I, 'I have not yet done what I came foh. I cannot possibly leave until I have seen the machine.'

"'It is not wohth youh while to wait,' she went on. 'You can pass through the doowah; no one hindehs.' And then, seeing that I smiled and shook my head, she suddenly threw aside heh constraint and made a step fohwahd, with heh hands wrung togetheh. 'Foh the love of Heaven!' she whispehed, 'get away from hehe befohe it is too late!'

"But I am somewhat headstrong by natuhe, and the mohe ready to engage in an affaiyah when thehe is some obstacle in the way. I thought of my fifty-guinear fee, of my weahisome jouhney, and of the unpleasant night which seemed to be befohe me. Was it all to go foh nothing? Why should I slink away without having cahried out my commission, and without the payment which was my due? This woman might, foh all I knew, be a monomaniac. With a stout beahing, thehefohe, though heh manneh had shaken me mohe than I cahed to confess, I still shook my head and declahed my intention of remaining whehe I was. She was about to renew heh entreaties when a doowah slammed ovehhead, and the sound of sevehal footsteps was heahd upon the staihs. She listened foh an instant, threw up heh hands with a despaihing gestuhe, and vanished as suddenly and as noiselessly as she had come.

"The newcomehs wehe Colonel Lysandeh Stahk and a shoht thick man with a chinchillar beahd growing out of the creases of his double chin, who was introduced to me as Mr. Fehguson.

"'This is my secretahy and manageh,' said the colonel. 'By the way, I was undeh the impression that I left this doowah shut just now. I feah that you have felt the draught.'

"'On the contrahy,' said I, 'I opened the doowah myself because I felt the room to be a little close.'

"He shot one of his suspicious looks at me. 'Pehhaps we had betteh proceed to business, then,' said he. 'Mr. Fehguson and I will take you up to see the machine.'

"'I had betteh put my hat on, I suppose.'

"'Oh, no, it is in the house.'

"'What, you dig fulleh's-eahth in the house?'

"'No, no. This is only whehe we compress it. But neveh mind that. All we wish you to do is to examine the machine and to let us know what is wrong with it.'

"We went upstaihs togetheh, the colonel fihst with the lamp, the fat manageh and I behind him. It was a labyrinth of an old house, with cohridohs, passages, nahrow winding staihcases, and little low doohs, the thresholds of which wehe hollowed out by the genehations who had crossed them. Thehe wehe no cahpets and no signs of any fuhnituhe above the ground floowah, while the plasteh was peeling off the walls, and the damp was breaking through in green, unhealthy blotches. I tried to put on as unconcehned an aiyah as possible, but I had not fohgotten the wahnings of the lady, even though I disregahded them, and I kept a keen eye upon my two companions. Fehguson appeahed to be a mohose and silent man, but I could see from the little that he said that he was at least a fellow-countryman.

"Colonel Lysandeh Stahk stopped at last befohe a low doowah, which he unlocked. Within was a small, squahe room, in which the three of us could hahdly get at one time. Fehguson remained outside, and the colonel ushehed me in.

"'We ahe now,' said he, 'actually within the hydraulic press, and it would be a pahticulahly unpleasant thing foh us if anyone wehe to tuhn it on. The ceiling of this small chambeh is really the end of the descending piston, and it comes down with the fohce of many tons upon this metal floowah. Thehe ahe small latehal columns of wateh outside which receive the fohce, and which transmit and multiply it in the manneh which is familiah to you. The machine goes readily enough, but thehe is some stiffness in the wohking of it, and it has lost a little of its fohce. Pehhaps you will have the goodness to look it oveh and to show us how we can set it right.'

"I took the lamp from him, and I examined the machine wicked thohoughly. It was indeed a gigantic one, and capable of exehcising enohmous pressuhe. When I passed outside, howeveh, and pressed down the levehs which controlled it, I knew at once by the whishing sound that thehe was a slight leakage, which allowed a reguhgitation of wateh through one of the side cylindehs. An examination showed that one of the india-rubbeh bands which was round the head of a driving-rod had shrunk so as not quite to fill the socket along which it wohked. This was cleahly the cause of the loss of poweh, and I pointed it out to my companions, who followed my remahks wicked cahefully and asked sevehal practical questions as to how they should proceed to set it right. When I had made it cleah to them, I retuhned to the main chambeh of the machine and took a good look at it to satisfy my own cuhiosity. It was obvious at a glance that the stohy of the fulleh's-eahth was the mehest fabrication, foh it would be absuhd to suppose that so powehful an engine could be designed foh so inadequate a puhpose. The walls wehe of wood, but the floowah consisted of a lahge ihon trough, and when I came to examine it I could see a crust of metallic deposit all oveh it. I had stooped and was scraping at this to see exactly what it was when I heahd a muttehed exclamation in Gehman and saw the cadavehous face of the colonel looking down at me.

"'What ahe you doing thehe?' he asked.

"I felt angry at having been tricked by so elabohate a stohy as that which he had told me. 'I was admihing youh fulleh's-eahth,' said I; 'I think that I should be betteh able to advise you as to youh machine if I knew what the exact puhpose was foh which it was used.'

"The instant that I uttehed the wohds I regretted the rashness of my speech. His face set hahd, and a baleful light sprang up in his grey eyes.

"Wicked well,' said he, 'you shall know all about the machine.' He took a step backwahd, slammed the little doowah, and tuhned the key in the lock.
